Central Executive Committee 76th Standing Meeting 68

At 3 PM on the 24th, the 76th Standing Committee meeting of the Central Executive Committee was held. Ye Chucang, Hu Hanmin, Tan Yankai, and Sun Ke attended. Li Wenfan, Jiao Yitang, Liu Jiwen, Gui Chongji, Chen Lifu, Shao Yuanchong, Ke Xing'e, Enke Baturu, Ma Chaojun, He Yingqin, Gu Yingfen, Zeng Yangfu, Liu Luyin, and Wang Zhengting were present. Chairman Tan Yankai presided over the meeting. The resolutions are as follows: (1) The 4th, 15th, 16th, 17th, 21st, 23rd, 25th, 26th, 27th, 28th, 45th, 51st, and 53rd Divisions of the Army, and the 2nd and 4th Group Armies are all reactionary troops. In addition, the 34th, 44th, and 52nd Divisions of the Army and the 22nd Army and other troops have been reorganized. All special party departments of the relevant armies and divisions should be abolished. (2) Revised the outlines of the election law for provincial representatives' congresses, Articles 2 and 5, the outlines of the organization law for provincial representatives' congresses, Articles 1, 2, 3, and 4, the outlines of the election law for provincial executive committees and supervisory committees, Articles 1 and 2, the outlines of the election law for county representatives' congresses, Articles 1 and 2, the outlines of the organization law for county representatives' congresses, Articles 1, 2, 3, and 4, and the outlines of the election law for county executive committees and supervisory committees, Articles 1, 2, and 3, and changed the title of the outline of the election law for provincial representatives' congresses to the outline of the election law for representatives to the provincial representatives' congresses, and changed the title of the outline of the election law for county representatives' congresses to the outline of the election law for representatives to the county representatives' congresses. (3) Approved the names and numbers of the aircraft purchased with donations from overseas Chinese (second batch).

Norwegian Envoy Presents Credentials

The newly appointed Norwegian Minister Olberg, accompanied by one staff member, went to the National Government to meet with Chairman Chiang at 11 AM on the 24th to present his credentials. The ceremony was the same as that for previous ministers presenting their credentials. The text of the address and reply are recorded below.

Address Your Excellency the Chairman, The Minister, honored to be commissioned by His Majesty the King of my country as Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary to China, is honored to present today my Letter of Credence, and the Letter of Recall of the former Minister, Mr. Michelsen. I am pleased and delighted to be on this mission to your country, and there is no need to elaborate. The friendship between Norway and China is already profound, and I will do my best to further strengthen this friendship and make it permanent. Furthermore, having been entrusted with this mission, I will be conscientious and sincere, and strive to cooperate with your government to maintain the best friendship between the two countries and make it more intimate day by day. This is the common wish of the government of my country and the government of your country. On behalf of His Majesty the King of my country, I respectfully wish your country prosperity and your Chairman good health.

Reply Your Excellency the Minister, I am pleased to receive your Letter of Credence as Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary to the Republic of China, commissioned by His Majesty the King of your country, and the Letter of Recall of the former Minister, with much joy. Your Excellency has always expressed sympathy for the Chinese people. The friendly relations between China and Norway have always been extremely cordial, as Your Excellency has stated. This Chairman deeply believes that from now on, the friendship between our two countries will become more intimate, and the National Government will do its best to cooperate with Your Excellency to fully realize this. On behalf of the Republic of China and its citizens, I respectfully wish His Majesty the King of your country good health and the people of your country peace and prosperity.

Commemorative Week for the Central Committee and National Government 69

Central Party Headquarters: At 9 AM on the 24th, the Central Party Headquarters held the 48th Sun Yat-sen Memorial Week in the auditorium. Approximately 500-600 people attended, including members of the Central Committee, officials from various departments and commissions, and guests. Chairman Hu Hanmin gave a report after the ceremony, stating that during the last memorial week, Committee Member Wu Zhihui reported that Yan Xishan's recent proposals were meaningless and would not gain the sympathy of the people. He expected the situation to calm down within a week. However, based on his observation, whether this would happen depended on Yan's ability to come to his senses. Yan's actions were a double-edged sword, due to his weak understanding of the party's and government's systems and responsibilities. He was easily tempted by external forces and acted inconsistently. Despite repeated corrections from the Central Committee and rebukes from the public, he continued to defend himself with fragmented and incomprehensible reasons, revealing his premeditation. As a member of the Central Committee and the National Government, Yan should bear significant responsibility for the party and the country. However, shortly after arriving in Nanjing, he returned to his old feudal base, fortified his forces, and violated the demobilization plan approved at the conference. What was his intention? He smugly believed that his violation of party rule was a clever move, but public opinion largely saw it as a path to self-destruction. Yan was usually adept at reading the political climate and exploiting situations. He was like a revolving lantern warlord who could maintain his power through cunning regardless of the circumstances, ultimately using and deceiving others to his advantage. However, his current situation had become a narrow pass. He had gained the support of the Northwest Army, the Anfu clique, the Reconstructionists, the Nationalists, and the imperialists who had always hoped for a divided China. He was no longer in control and was now bound by the conditions set by these factions, unable to hide his intentions. Any attempt to escape would lead to his downfall. Having always exploited others, he would likely be exploited this time. The Central Committee had only resorted to force against past rebels as a last resort. Whether peace could be achieved this time depended on Yan's ability to break free from his environment and abandon his feudal ideology. If he remained obstinate and destructive to the party and the country, the Central Committee would be unable to maintain peace, and he would likely disintegrate before the arrival of the punitive forces. The meeting adjourned at 10:30 AM after the report.

National Government: At 10 AM on the same day, the National Government held Sun Yat-sen Memorial Week. Attendees included Chiang Kai-shek, Tan Yankai, Gu Yingfen, He Yingqin, Zhu Peide, Chen Yi, Yi Peiji, Niu Yongjian, He Yaotsu, Chen Shaokuan, Wang Jun, Xia Douyin, Zhang Jingjiang, Shao Yuanchong, Yang Jie, Zhang Zhijiang, Zhang Nanxian, Wu Xingya, Wang Zhengting, Liu Jiwen, and officials above the level of section chiefs from various departments and commissions, as well as staff from the civil service and military affairs departments of the National Government, totaling over 300 people. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek presided. Secretary Qian Changzhao delivered the following political report: "The recent unrest in the country is due to Yan Xishan's absurd remarks. I have said before that the people are easily agitated, and those in positions of power should be especially cautious. Yan has always been known for his prudence, as proven by history. Since the founding of the Republic, there have been many political upheavals, such as Yuan Shikai's attempt to become emperor, Puyi's restoration, and the dictatorships of Feng Guozhang, Duan Qirui, and Cao Kun. Yan has always been steady and able to cope with various situations, maintaining his position and ensuring the safety of Shanxi. He deserves to be called a man who understands the times. Now that our military operations have ended and the Central Committee is focusing on improving governance, Yan has suddenly issued a series of telegrams, advocating for courtesy in running the country, convening the Third Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee, and establishing a Privy Council and Marshal's Office. These ideas are bewildering. Yet, he believes that his proposals are a practical way to save the party and the country. Yan's telegrams mention 'abandoning food' and 'losing sleep at night.' It is unimaginable that the practical solutions he has come up with after abandoning food and losing sleep are so irrational. There is no need to elaborate on their irrationality, as there have been many criticisms from various quarters. However, Yan's remarks have caused unrest and social turmoil, and his attempt to stop the chaos has only created more chaos. We find it strange that Yan, who was cautious when dealing with local affairs in Shanxi, is now so careless about the overall situation of the country. He was able to handle difficult circumstances well in the past, but now he cannot set aside his prejudices towards the Central Committee, which is determined to improve governance. Is it because Yan's position has risen recently, so his courage has grown? Or is it because Yan is too loyal and enthusiastic towards the Central Committee, so he expresses himself arbitrarily without distinguishing right from wrong? Only Yan himself knows the answer. The Central Committee has always pursued a policy of peaceful unification. When rebellions occurred last year, from the Guangxi clique to Tang Shengzhi, we always tried to stop the unrest and adopt a lenient approach. Only when it became impossible to stop did we resort to suppression. In short, we only use force as a last resort, and we use it for the safety of the party and the country, not for personal gain. However, Yan's telegrams mention 'holding the flag of the Blue Sky with a White Sun together, being party soldiers together, and fighting each other, with the casualties being our armed comrades.' How can he not distinguish between obedience and rebellion? And the claim that force is used for personal gain is a deliberate slander. Even though he has made repeated mistakes, the Central Committee will sincerely correct him. Although we have received reports that Yan is preparing for war, the Central Committee will still appeal to him with righteousness, hoping that he will pull back from the brink. In reality, Yan has two smooth paths to take: first, withdraw his resignation and serve the party and the country wholeheartedly, implementing demobilization; second, sincerely retire and go abroad to clarify his intentions. A true man should act with integrity. If he is anxious about gains and losses and uses retreat as a way to advance, he will lose his revolutionary character. If Yan can thoroughly realize this, it is not too late. But if he chooses to take risks, it will be detrimental to the party and the country, as well as to himself. The above is regarding Yan. As for the future of the revolution, I also have some suggestions. We are not afraid of the invasion of imperialists, the existence of feudal ideology, or the machinations of frustrated politicians and warlords. The most dangerous and painful thing is the disintegration of the revolutionary forces themselves. Since the Northern Expedition, some revolutionaries have deteriorated, some have become corrupt, and some have lost sight of the big picture and engaged in destructive work in opposition simply because they disagree with the authorities. The revolution cannot succeed because of this, and the reactionaries are able to become rampant because of this. In short, the more the revolutionary forces disintegrate, the more the reactionaries dance with joy and have opportunities to sow discord. The reason why the revolution has not completely failed today is that there is still a group of forces fighting tirelessly, regardless of sacrifice. This fighting force is where the lifeline of the party and the country lies and should be cherished. At the same time, we hope that those who have a considerable history with the revolution should immediately turn back and work for the party and the country, even if they have taken the wrong path. Then, the bad environment will be easily broken, and the revolution will be easily successful."

The Ministry of Interior Plans a Draft Marriage Law 70

Submitted to the Executive Yuan and forwarded to the Legislative Yuan for review

Yang Zhaotai, the Minister of the Interior, previously ordered the Committee on Rituals, Systems, and Attire to expedite the finalization of the four rites (marriage, mourning, sacrifice, and audience) plan so that it could be submitted to the Central Government for promulgation and implementation. Upon receiving the order, the committee immediately proceeded and first drafted the marriage and mourning rites. After review and approval by Minister Yang, it was submitted to the Executive Yuan yesterday to be forwarded to the Legislative Yuan for review and approval. The draft consists of twelve sections for marriage rites and eighteen sections for mourning rites. It is said that it was mainly drafted by Committee Member Yin Guangxun. The full text is quite lengthy because each section is accompanied by explanations. Given the great importance of this matter to public customs and culture, the original text of each section of the marriage rites is listed below, with the explanations omitted to save space.

Section 1: Engagement. Marriage should only be considered when the man and woman reach adulthood. First, an intermediary should inquire about the consent of both the man and woman. The parents or a relative within the fourth degree of kinship should be in charge.

Section 2: Betrothal. If consent is given, the man's representative should provide a written document stating the family history, lineage, and the name, birth year, month, and day of the suitor. No more than four gifts and articles of clothing should be prepared. An intermediary should be sent to the woman's family. The woman's representative should welcome them in, and the guest should present the written document and gifts. The representative bows, and the representative accepts the document with a bow. The guest asks to await their response, and the representative takes the document inside and prepares a reply in the style of the original. The reply is presented with a bow, and the guest receives the document with two bows. The guest is then treated with regular courtesy. The guest departs, and the representative sees them off at the gate with a bow. The guest returns to report to the man's representative. If this is done in a public place, the exchange of documents and gifts is the same, and the guest is treated with courtesy.

Section 3: Setting the Date. When a date for the marriage is set, the man's representative should send a letter to the woman's representative stating: "So-and-so respectfully accepts your gracious favor and has chosen a propitious day in the coming month to hold the wedding ceremony. We respectfully request your consent." The woman's representative should reply: "We acknowledge the auspicious date and respectfully agree." The letter should be written on red paper or follow other appropriate customs.

Section 4: Preparing the Guests. Prior to the ceremony, guests should be prepared. A respected and influential person should be selected as the wedding officiant. The intermediary and attendants should be invited next, and relatives and friends should be notified of the date and invited to witness the ceremony.

Section 5: The Wedding Procession. On the appointed day, a location should be set up in the main hall, decorated with flags and streamers. The number of musical instruments is not fixed. There should be one carriage each for the groom and bride, decorated as appropriate. They should all wait outside the gate. The host and the groom should be in formal attire. The host leads the groom to his place and pays respects to the ancestors with three bows. The host instructs the woman, and the woman bows to receive the instructions. The groom arrives outside the gate and alights from the carriage. The representative comes out to greet him and escorts him to the hall. The representative faces west, and the groom faces north and bows three times. They take their seats briefly. The music plays. The representative escorts the groom up to the hall. The bride's attendants escort the bride out. The groom bows and exits. The bride boards the carriage, and the groom also boards the carriage. They are led forward.

Section 6: The Wedding Ceremony. The carriage arrives at the gate, and the groom alights. The groom is led in, and the attendants greet them outside the gate and escort them up to the hall. They are presented with flowers. The groom faces east, and the bride faces west, standing side by side facing north. The master of ceremonies invites the wedding officiant to take his place, facing south. The host, intermediary, relatives, and guests take their places in order. The intermediary presents the wedding certificate. The wedding officiant reads it aloud, and the groom and bride add their seals. The intermediary, host, and wedding officiant add their seals in order. If the bride's host is not present, they may add their seal first and wait. The groom faces west, and the bride faces east, standing opposite each other. They bow three times each. The attendants exchange their decorations and face north again. The wedding officiant delivers a congratulatory speech, the host delivers an instructive speech, the intermediary describes the course of the wedding, the guests offer congratulations, and the host expresses gratitude. The groom and bride thank the wedding officiant with three bows, and the wedding officiant steps aside to return the courtesy. The guests retire, and the host leads the people to the hall.

Section 7: Nuptial Cup Ceremony. The master of ceremonies instructs the attendants to lead the bride to the room with candles. The music plays. The groom leads the way, followed by the attendants. A seat is set up in the room, with seven pairs of chopsticks and wine and food prepared. The groom faces west, and the bride faces east. The attendants take the wine and offer it to the groom and then to the bride, symbolizing harmony. Each finishes their drink and leaves the seat. The attendants exit.

Section 8: Audience. The hall is set up as before. The parents-in-law are seated facing southeast. The groom and bride come out in formal attire to meet them and bow three times facing north. They then meet the other senior relatives in order, bowing three times each. They bow once to relatives of equal status. Those of lower status bow once to the groom and bride. If the maternal grandparents-in-law are present, they should be met before the senior relatives, with the same ceremony as meeting the parents-in-law. The relatives of both families bow to each other once.

Section 9: Bride's Feast. The bride is feasted in the hall, facing east and west, with seven pairs of chopsticks and wine and food prepared. The mother-in-law offers the bride food, and she bows twice to accept it. The mother-in-law returns to the room to rest, and the feast ends.

Section 10: Honoring the Guests. The guests are honored. Male guests are in the outer hall, and female guests are in the main hall. The host personally pours wine to pay respect, bowing after pouring. The guests return the courtesy. After three rounds of wine, the groom and bride come out to honor the guests. The guests all stand up, and the groom and bride face the seats and bow together. The groom and bride retire, and the guests finish their drinks and the feast ends. The guests depart, and the representative sees them off at the gate. If this is done in a public place, the groom and bride return together after the guests leave, and the representatives return to their respective homes.

Section 11: Ancestral Worship. The day after the wedding, the hall is set up as before, with incense, flowers, wine, and fruit. The parents-in-law lead the groom and bride to see the ancestors, all in formal attire. The parents-in-law stand in front, and the groom and bride follow behind, bowing three times and saying, "So-and-so's son and so-and-so's wife, So-and-so, have come to pay their respects." The son bows three times. The parents-in-law retire, and the groom and bride also retire.

Section 12: Meeting the Maternal Grandparents-in-Law. On an auspicious day, the groom and bride dress formally and take gifts to meet the maternal grandparents-in-law. The host is formally dressed in the hall. The groom and bride enter the hall together and bow three times to the maternal grandparents-in-law. Other relatives are met in order, following the proper etiquette. The host entertains the groom as appropriate. The groom and bride exit, and the host sees them off at the gate with a bow.

Jiangsu Province Implements the Abolition of the Baojia System 71

The Department of Civil Affairs issues an order to all counties to comply

Miao Bin, the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs of Jiangsu Province, believing that the Baojia system harassed the people and hindered political training, specially requested the provincial government to abolish it and transfer the duties of the Baojia to the township and town offices. This was approved by the provincial government. The text of the Department's report to the provincial government and the order to the county magistrates are recorded below.

Report to the Provincial Government: This office investigated and found that on October 5 of last year, Decree No. 6084 from the Provincial Government stated that the County Magistrate of Rugao reported that the Baojia system harassed the people and hindered political training, listing the harms and proposing to abolish it by issuing a general order. The Government ordered that the matter be verified and a response be awaited. Upon receiving this order, it was determined that the local conditions in each county might differ, and it was necessary to determine whether there would be any practical obstacles to issuing a general order to abolish the Baojia system at this time. A report was first submitted to the Provincial Government, and orders were issued to the county magistrates to investigate and report. Now, the counties have successively submitted their reports to the Department, and their reports can be divided into six categories: (1) Those that have already abolished the system, including Jiangyin, Fengxian, Lianshui, and Jiading; (2) Those that advocate for abolition and believe there are no obstacles, such as Rugao, Nantong, Pixian, and Suqian; (3) Those that advocate for abolition after local self-government work has been completed, which can be further divided into two subcategories: (a) Abolition after township and town organizations are established and the duties of the Baojia are assigned to someone, such as Chuansha, Jinshan, Qidong, Yangzhou, Jiangdu, Changshu, Yizheng, Songjiang, Donghai, Baoshan, Nanhui, and Jurong, totaling thirteen counties; (b) Abolition after the Lilin organizations are established, such as Taixing and Xinghua, totaling two counties; (4) Those that advocate for gradual abolition, such as Wuxian, Danyang, and Siyang, totaling three counties; (5) Those that advocate for transforming the Baojia into clerks of the township and town offices or township police, district detectives, or Lilin chiefs, such as Gaoyou, Yancheng, Chongming, Haimen, Funing, and Gan'yu, totaling six counties; (6) Those that advocate for postponing the abolition, such as Zhenjiang, Shanghai, Jintan, Taicang, and Wujiang, totaling five counties. To summarize the opinions of the counties, it can be considered that a majority favor the abolition of the Baojia system. Although Zhenjiang and the other four counties advocate for postponing the abolition, their reason is that they are concerned that the original duties of the Baojia will not be assumed by anyone if the Baojia are suddenly abolished. However, since counties such as Jiangyin have already abolished the system without any obstacles, and the townships and towns in each county have now been organized, the original duties of the Baojia will not be a problem after the abolition. This Department proposes to transfer the duties of the Baojia to the township and town offices and issue a general order to abolish this harmful system as soon as possible to avoid harassing the people and hindering political training. Are the reasons for the prompt abolition of the Baojia system and the transfer of the original duties of the Baojia to the township and town offices appropriate? A clear report is being prepared, excerpting the views of each county and compiling them into a folded report, which is being submitted to you for your examination.

Order to the County Magistrates: Order No. 740 of the Provincial Government stated that, regarding the Department's report on whether to abolish the Baojia system, a folded report containing the opinions of each county was prepared, proposing to transfer the original duties of the Baojia to the township and town offices and issue a general order to abolish this harmful system as soon as possible to avoid harassing the people and hindering political training. The 263rd meeting of the committee resolved to handle it as proposed, and the Department of Civil Affairs was ordered to comply. In addition to issuing separate orders, the original report is hereby copied and issued to you, the County Magistrate, for your compliance and reporting without delay.

The Reorganization Plan of the Northeast Fleet 72

Qingdao Correspondence: Shen Honglie, the Commander of the Northeast Navy, has recently proposed the following reorganization plan due to the loss of three ships (Jiangzhen, Jiangli, etc.) in the Second Fleet during the war against Russia last year, as well as significant losses in the Marine Corps: (1) Repair damaged and old ships. The Jiangzhen and Jiangli, etc., have sunk and not yet been salvaged. Shen plans to salvage and repair them after the river thaws. All the unrepaired ships in the First and Second Fleets will also be repaired. It is reported that Shen has requested 400,000 yuan from the Commander of the Northeast Border Defense for these expenses. (2) Reorganize the Marine Corps. Shen believes that the Marine Corps needs to be reorganized urgently. He has decided to reorganize the existing teams into five independent battalions to achieve uniformity. (3) Train officers and sailors of each team. The officers and sailors of each warship and the Marine Corps have been patrolling and defending for many years and have not been trained for a long time. Shen plans to transfer the soldiers of each fleet to Qingdao and Liaoning in batches for training. It is reported that Shen will come to Qingdao at the end of February to reorganize the First Fleet after making some arrangements in Liaoning. (February 22)

Japanese Establish Police Stations in Qingdao Without Authorization 73

The Qingdao City Party Committee requests the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to protest

When Qingdao was recovered in 1922, the Japanese established a police station inside their consulate and set up posts at various locations for patrols. At that time, Xiong Bingqi, the Director-General of Jiaozhou, negotiated with the Japanese consul many times, ordering them to stop, but to no effect. For the past seven years, the Japanese police have been arresting people without authorization and acting recklessly. The authorities have turned a blind eye. Earlier this month, a Chinese man named Liu Jiwen, who worked as a servant in a Japanese household, was arrested by the Japanese police on suspicion of theft and subjected to torture. The Second District Party Committee has requested the City Party Committee to send a letter to the Municipal Government to protest to the Japanese consul and forward it to the Central Government, instructing the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate seriously with the Japanese ambassador to cancel the unauthorized establishment of police stations by the Japanese. The City Party Committee has already done so. The text of its report to the Central Government is as follows: (According to the report from the Executive Committee of the Second District Association, the case of the Japanese police arbitrarily arresting our citizen Liu Jiwen is a violation of our national rights and an insult to our national dignity. At a time when the Central Government is implementing the abolition of consular jurisdiction, this abnormal event has occurred in this city, which is especially hateful. Please forward a letter to the Municipal Government, strongly protesting to the Japanese consul, stating that Liu Jiwen should be handled by our courts and that the Japanese consul should be notified that they are not allowed to establish illegal Japanese police stations in this city. Please expedite the forwarding of a letter to the Municipal Government, making a reasoned case to the Japanese consul to uphold the Central Government's authority and protect the safety of the citizens. Based on this, it has been found that since the withdrawal of the Japanese army from Qingdao, Japanese police have been patrolling with weapons in the main streets of the city and in the Cangku and Sifang areas. A letter has been sent to the Municipal Government to protest to the Japanese consul. At a time when the abolition of consular jurisdiction is being vigorously promoted, the Japanese police are still recklessly arresting Chinese citizens. This is intolerable. Where is national sovereignty? Based on the aforementioned situation, in addition to sending a letter to the Municipal Government to promptly investigate and negotiate the Liu Jiwen case, the unauthorized establishment of police stations by the Japanese in Qingdao and the encroachment on national rights are reported to you for your review and forwarding to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for a serious protest in order to maintain national rights. This is for the convenience of the Party. (February 20)

Japanese Police Arrest People in Xiamen Again 74

The Siming Steering Committee requests serious negotiations

Xiamen Correspondence: Japan, based on the Twenty-One Demands, established a police station in Wutongcheng, Xiamen, in 1916. After repeated negotiations by the government, it was nominally abolished, but in fact, only the police station sign was removed. The plainclothes police remained as before. In 1928, the arrest of a Korean youth, Li Guihuan, caused fierce resistance from the people of Xiamen and became an international negotiation. As a result, the Japanese consul agreed to abolish the Wutongcheng police station. It was not until the winter of last year that it was moved to the Taiwan Public Association in Wuzhiding. In reality, it was not abolished. On the 14th of this month, Nakajima, the chief of the Japanese police station, led five or six Japanese policemen to search the Southeast Restaurant, which is owned by Taiwanese people of Japanese nationality, on Siming North Road. The First District Police Station of the Public Security Bureau, upon hearing the report, sent officer Wu Youkang with the police to investigate. When they arrived, the Japanese police had already left. Unexpectedly, Nakajima returned to search the residence of Li Longxi, a shareholder of the restaurant, and arrested Li, taking him to the Taiwan Public Association police station. At 4 PM, Li was sent to the Japanese Consulate on Gulangyu. After this incident occurred, the Siming County Steering Committee immediately sent letters to the Zhangzhou-Xiamen Naval Police Headquarters and the County Government, requesting serious negotiations. The original letter is as follows: (Regarding the report that the Japanese police in Xiamen arbitrarily sent several detectives to the Southeast Restaurant on Siming North Road at 2 PM on the 14th of this month to arrest Taiwanese Li Longxi, who was taken to the police station for interrogation and sent to the Japanese Consulate on Gulangyu at 4 PM for punishment, Xiamen is entirely our country's territory. On March 2, 1927, the police arbitrarily arrested Korean Li Guihuan, which became the March 2nd case negotiation. The pain of that incident remains. At that time, the Japanese consul declared that the police had voluntarily disbanded and that the same behavior would not occur again. Now, without notifying our government officials, they deliberately arrest people in our territory in broad daylight and send them to Gulangyu. Their contempt for our sovereignty and insult to our national dignity are even more obvious than in the March 2nd case and are utterly infuriating. In addition to sending separate letters, we are sending this letter to your Commander and County Magistrate, requesting that you investigate and negotiate seriously to protect our sovereignty and maintain our national dignity. We also hope to receive a reply, for the sake of party friendship.

Fu Bandits Rampant in Zhangzhou 75

Xiamen Correspondence: The Fu Zaihui bandits, who have the nature of the Boxers, have fled into the Shanchong area of Tong'an County after being pursued and suppressed by Zhang Zhen's First Division. They gathered four or five hundred people, led by the bandit leader Wu Ci, and occupied the important town of Guankou, which lies between Tong'an and Zhangzhou, on the morning of the 17th, raising the banner of [General Wu of Jiangnan of the Great Ming]. The town only had some local militia and a dozen policemen from the county's Public Security Bureau branch. Although they resisted slightly, they were no match for the enemy due to their small numbers. Four members of the militia and three policemen from the Public Security Bureau were killed on the spot. After entering the town, the bandits extorted 20,000 yuan from the merchants and demanded that it be paid by the evening of the 18th, or the entire town would be burned down. On the evening of the 17th, they collected over 1,000 yuan. On the 18th, Wu led more than 80 of his followers to Jiaowei to surround and confiscate the militia's firearms. On the way back, they were ambushed at the Hongdai Bridge by Yan's regiment of the 167th Brigade of the 56th Division, which was heading to Quanzhou from Zhangzhou. Five or six bandits were killed. After Wu Ci's defeat, he returned to Guankou and feared that the 56th Division would pursue them, so they abandoned Guankou that night and retreated to the Daling Mountains. On the 19th, Yan's regiment entered Guankou, and Wu fled to Lindun. When the Fu bandits occupied Guankou, the residents fled to Xiamen. According to the refugees, in addition to the [General Wu of Jiangnan of the Great Ming] banner, the bandits also had banners such as [Nine Heavens Profound Lady] and [Xuantian Emperor]. Their internal organization is similar to that of the Sanhehui bandits. Most of them are from Longyan and Zhangzhou. They wear blue or black clothing and carry a bamboo amulet around their waists. The core bandits are mostly key figures in the Sanhehui. The group that occupied Guankou this time is the same group that recently fled to Changtai after being severely suppressed by the First Division in Zhangzhou. During their two-day occupation of Guankou, the bandits looted and extorted, causing losses of over 20,000 yuan. (February 21)

Important News 2

Naval Inspection Delegation's Arrival in the United States 77

Mr. Du Xigui's naval inspection delegation departed from Yokohama on the Japanese Mail Steamship Company's Asama Maru on December 30th and arrived in Honolulu at 2 PM on the 27th. The ship docked for 24 hours. Consul Huang Yunsu of that port, along with the chairman of the local branch of the Chinese Nationalist Party and the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, boarded the ship to welcome them. They were guided to tour the scenic spots of the city. In the evening, the Consul, the Party branch, and the Chamber of Commerce hosted a public banquet. Representatives were also sent from the local naval port to pay their respects. The next day, they visited Pearl Harbor (naval port) to return the greetings and took a car tour of the docks, factories, and airfield. The port employs over two hundred Chinese as staff, workers, and artisans, which is quite a unique feature. They then returned to the ship, and the ship departed again at around 11 AM. On January 2nd, at 9 PM, they arrived in San Francisco. Zhang Qian, our country's Consul General in San Francisco, the chairman of the Chinese Consolidated Benevolent Association, the president of the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce, representatives from the General Branch of the Nationalist Party, reporters from Chinese and foreign newspapers, representatives from the local army and navy, the mayor's representative, the police chief, and the fire chief boarded the ship to meet them. They then disembarked and toured Chinatown. Afterward, they went to the Chinese Consolidated Benevolent Association, where Consul General Zhang invited Mr. Du to give a speech. They then went to the Nationalist Party branch for a discussion and then attended banquets held by various groups before returning to the hotel. The next day, they visited the Mare Island Naval Shipyard and other locations. On the 5th, they went to Lawson, accompanied by Consul General Zhang. On the 6th, they visited the San Pedro Naval Base to see battleships. On the 8th, the US Navy sent Major Smith to the hotel to guide them to visit the airfield. At noon, the American Chamber of Commerce hosted a banquet. In the afternoon, they attended a tea party hosted by the Chinese Chamber of Commerce and visited a commercial airplane manufacturing plant. In the evening, they attended a banquet at a Chinese restaurant hosted by the Chamber of Commerce. There were many Chinese and foreign naval and military figures and overseas Chinese in attendance, making it a grand occasion. On the 9th, they visited submarine tenders, destroyers, and new-style repair ships. The ships' scale and equipment were very complete. In the afternoon, they visited the Marine Corps and the Naval Hospital. They traveled back to Lawson by car that night. On the 10th, they took a train to Chicago, arriving at the port at 9 AM on the 13th. They toured the city of Chicago for three hours and then took a train to Washington, arriving at the station at 8 AM on the 14th. Minister Wu came to greet them, and they went to the hotel to rest. On the 15th, they met with the Acting Secretary of State, the Acting Secretary of the Navy, and the Chief of Naval Operations. In the evening, they attended a dinner hosted by Minister Wu. The Navy sent Major Cajun to be in charge of reception. On the morning of the 16th, they visited the Hydrographic Office. In the afternoon, they visited the US President with Minister Wu. In the evening, they attended a tea party at the embassy, with over 600 foreign guests attending. On the morning of the 17th, they visited a cannon factory. In the afternoon, they visited the Naval Academy. On the 18th, they visited the aircraft testing ground. In the afternoon, they laid wreaths at the Tomb of the Unknown Soldier and the Washington Monument and visited Washington's former residence. In the evening, they attended a tea party at the British Embassy in the United States. On Sunday the 19th, they toured the Washington Monument, the Lincoln Memorial Hall, and the Art Institute. On the morning of the 20th, they toured the National Museum and the Library of Congress. On the 20th, they visited the gun testing range. The range was well-organized, and all naval guns, artillery, ammunition, steel plates, and aircraft bombs were tested there. On the 21st, they visited a chemical military supplies factory. The factory specializes in the production of protective gas masks and various poisonous gases, which have been greatly improved since the European War. On the morning of the 22nd, they visited the Naval Observatory. In the evening, they were invited to a banquet by US Navy Admiral Hughes. On the afternoon of the 23rd, the British Naval Attaché in the United States hosted a lunch. It is rumored that the naval inspection team will leave Washington that afternoon and, after inspecting various important naval locations along the way, will travel to England on a German ship from New York on February 1st.

Local Correspondence

Songjiang 78

The Fugitive Bandit Leader is Escorted Back to Songjiang: The bandit Ji Lao Si and others, who were involved in the abduction of the young daughter of Jiao Shi Ru from Xinqiao Town in this county, escaped from prison in broad daylight last autumn during the handover of new and old prison staff. Subsequently, the county government offered a reward and ordered their arrest. Except for the bandit leader Ji Lao Si, the remaining criminals were apprehended successively and executed after approval. However, after Ji escaped, his bandit nature did not change, and he committed crimes in Nanhui, Shanghai, Pudong, and other places, hiding in the French Concession. The Detective Team of the Shanghai Special City Public Security Bureau investigated and, in cooperation with the French Concession police, arrested the bandit and escorted him back to the city Public Security Bureau to await review. After hearing the news, the county government immediately prepared a document and dispatched Political Police Chief Dong Futang to Shanghai to transfer him. At 4 PM on the 24th, the Shanghai Public Security Bureau also sent detectives to assist in escorting him back to Songjiang.

The New Prison Warden Takes Office: The newly appointed Prison Warden Zhang Zonglie was transferred from the Changshu County Prison. After the order was issued, he was unable to come immediately due to other matters. The duties of the county were temporarily assumed by Li Qinghe, appointed by the county government. Now, Mr. Zhang has come to Songjiang with his family yesterday and, after meeting with County Magistrate Jin, went to the prison to take office.

Provincial Order to Prepare for the Construction of Additional Prison Buildings: The number of prisoners in the county prison is increasing daily, gradually leading to insufficient capacity. The Higher Court sent personnel to Songjiang last year to investigate. After reporting back to the province, they issued a provincial order to construct an additional 20 prison buildings, instructing the county to discuss and implement the project. However, the expenses are enormous, and the local public funds have already been budgeted, making it impossible to allocate funds. This matter was raised at the 46th county government meeting. The meeting decided to convene various organizations on March 1st to discuss fundraising methods in order to comply with the order.

Fengxian 79

The Zhang Brothers are Falsely Accused of Theft: The brothers Zhang Er and Zhang San, farmers from Fang 20, Daijiaqiao, Eighth District, had a verbal dispute with the thief Qi Amao last year, which led to a long-standing feud. Unexpectedly, Qi held a grudge and, after being arrested as a suspect in his uncle's robbery case, fabricated accusations at the Tinglin Public Security Bureau, implicating the Zhang brothers. The bureau, together with the water police, came to Fengxian last month and arrested the Zhang brothers, escorting them to the Songjiang County Government for investigation. After interrogation, it was found that the accusations were false. At the same time, the neighbors also appealed and strongly vouched for them. Therefore, Songjiang County has sent personnel to investigate, and they should be released soon.

The Party Branch Intensifies Work: During this provincial inspection of the work of various departments, the Fengxian Party Branch was found to be the most sound and did not need reorganization. It was instructed to continue its work as usual. Therefore, the branch specially notified all subordinate party branches yesterday to intensify their work in order to fulfill their mission. Preparations for the county representative assembly are also underway, and instructions have been requested from the province, awaiting convocation.

The Branch Chief is Accused: Ma Teng, the chief of the Touqiao Public Security Branch, has been accused by citizens Feng Nanshan, Fan Xuegeng, Xu Yousan, and others of indulging thieves and imposing arbitrary fines for gambling and opium use. They have filed a complaint with the Department of Civil Affairs, instructing the county to investigate. County Magistrate Hong believed that the accusations fell under the jurisdiction of the judiciary and issued summonses. However, various organizations in the area stated that Branch Chief Ma had achieved some results in his work and that many of the accusations were unfounded. Therefore, they jointly vouched for him yesterday. Ma also claimed that he had been falsely accused and filed a countersuit requesting interrogation.

Kunshan 80

The Kidnapping Case at Xiajiaqiao: A family surnamed Wu in Xiajiaqiao, Kunshan County, was suddenly visited a few days ago by over twenty bandits speaking with a Jiangbei accent, who arbitrarily searched and robbed them. They stole silver dollars and clothing worth about three to four hundred yuan and kidnapped Wu Yingbao when they left. Afterwards, the victim reported the incident to Team Leader Li of the 12th Team of the Panshui Public Security, requesting that they pursue the fleeing bandits and rescue the hostage.

Suzhou 81

Gang of Bandits Invades Dianshan Lake: On the 21st of this month, Weijingtang Town in the county was robbed by a gang of bandits from Pudong. Team Leader Xu of the 11th Team of the 3rd District of the Water Police went to investigate. The shops that were robbed included Xie Changcheng, Shengtai, Tongtaixiang, Dayoukang, Zhou Daolai, Caishantang, Dayoucheng, Dafeng, Xietai, Dongmao, and the residence of Wang Guan. The losses were significant. Xiangmin Ge Quechunfu was killed by the bandits, and Water Police Officer Li Liang and team member Zhou Boyu were injured. After receiving treatment in Suzhou, they are no longer in danger. It is also known that the gang of bandits has fled to Dianshan Lake. The 11th and 12th teams of the Water Police have joined forces with the 2nd Team of the 1st District of the Water Police to pursue and suppress them.

Detective Team Captures Bandit Leader: A few days ago, the Qiantai Cheng wood shop in Zao City Street outside the Xumen gate was robbed by bandits. Officer Wang of the Seventh Sub-station of the Changmen gate arrested a bandit named Wei Zhihe and took him to the detective team for interrogation. According to his confession, he committed the robbery with the son of Jia Taiping, the owner of the Tongshunchang Guangfen mill. Jia's son has now fled to Shanghai. Based on the confession, Team Leader Zhou ordered detectives to go to Shanghai to arrest him. They arrested the bandit leader Guo Desheng at No. 94 Xintianxiang Lane, Beile Road, in the French Concession of Shanghai. The captured Wei Zhihe is a disciple of Guo. Guo had previously committed serious crimes, including destroying railways and robbing trains at Yaohuamen, and kidnapping Xu Fangting, the owner of the Wanshun Guangfen mill on Nanhao Street in this city last year. The bandit Guo Desheng was escorted from Shanghai to Suzhou yesterday (24th) and detained in the detective team for investigation.

Meeting to Widen Guanqian Street Main Road: Mayor Lu and Director Liu of the Public Works Bureau, in order to start widening Guanqian Street Road, specially convened commercial leaders and landlords of Guanqian at 2 PM yesterday in the abbot's room of the Xuanmiao Temple to discuss the widening of Guanqian Street main road. Mayor Lu chaired the meeting, reporting that the widening of Guanqian Street could not be delayed. The reconstruction of the stone road requires an expenditure of 24,527 yuan, while the budget for the 18th year is only 15,000 yuan. Therefore, opinions were specially sought. It was the consensus that the difference in funding was too great, and that construction would take two or three months, making it impossible for landlords to move temporarily, resulting in great losses. It was decided to appoint Shi Junqing, Wang Jiacang, and nine others to convene a road construction committee on March 1 to discuss long-term solutions. The Higher Court is actively progressing with the establishment of county courts in various counties. The Higher Court is establishing county courts in various locations. Wu Zengshan, the newly appointed president of the court in Wujin, is scheduled to officially take office on March 1. In Nantong, Dong Banggan was sent on the 24th to supervise the construction of the building. The other two locations, Songjiang and Jiangdu, will also be established. As for the Wuxi County Court, Wei, the secretary of the Higher Court, told reporters yesterday that there was no intention to postpone it. The original house purchased for the court was borrowed by the county Public Security Bureau and they refused to move. Initially, it was planned to relocate the court to the City God Temple, but the repair procedures were not easy. Therefore, a letter has been sent to the provincial government to negotiate, requesting that the Wuxi Public Security Bureau be ordered to move so that the site can be determined and construction can begin. In addition, the Higher Court is scheduled to recruit guard police officers today (25th), with a quota of 30, for the temporary detention center for prisoners in Shizikou. There are currently 150 applicants. Chen Ludan, a judicial investigator from the court, departed for the Shanghai area yesterday to investigate the judiciary in various counties.

The Suzhou Telephone Bureau is Actively Developing: Since Director Zhao took office at the Suzhou Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, he has actively sought development. Dongdai and other towns and villages in the county have already been connected to telephone lines one after another. Yesterday (24th), engineers were sent to Mudu City to lay telephone lines, and it is expected that they will be able to communicate with the city within about ten days. At the same time, personnel were sent to outside the Changmen gate to survey suitable locations and build branch bureaus, which are expected to be established within three months.

Qingpu 82

Forbidden from Seeing Her Lover, She Develops Suicidal Thoughts: A certain Jiang from a town in Qingpu County is in his twenties. His father owns a foreign goods store in Shanghai and is quite wealthy. However, Jiang likes gambling and does not work. In the spring of last year, his father, because of his incorrigible behavior, once declared in the newspaper that he was disowning him as his son. Jiang was forced to live temporarily at a friend's place. This spring, he was introduced by a friend to a position in a certain agency in the county, and he had some money in hand. Later, he met a girl named Aizhu, who was at the prime of her youth and quite beautiful. At first sight, they hated that they had not met sooner. Whenever they had free time, the two of them went to the park and were extraordinarily intimate, wishing to make a lifelong commitment to each other. This matter was heard by the girl's family. After investigating, they found out that Jiang's behavior was improper and were unwilling to agree to the marriage. Therefore, they imprisoned their daughter and cut off their contact. Jiang was frustrated and developed suicidal thoughts. At 7 PM the night before, he secretly took opium at his residence in an attempt to end his life. His roommate discovered this and immediately called a doctor for treatment. Fortunately, the rescue was timely, and he was saved.

Trying to Kidnap His Fiancée, He Mistakenly Kidnaps the Neighbor's Daughter: Feng Agou, a villager from Fengjiazhai, Qingpu County, was betrothed to A Jin, the second daughter of He Jinzhang, since childhood. Recently, He A Jin went to Shanghai to work as a servant. Her fiancé, Feng Agou, wanted to marry her but had no money. The other day, he learned that A Jin was coming home and gathered over ten fellow villagers that night to kidnap her. When they arrived at He's house, Feng knocked on the door and entered. Upon seeing a girl, he grabbed her. The others helped and they rushed out. Unexpectedly, the girl cried out loudly, "I am not He's daughter, why are you kidnapping me?" Upon hearing this, Feng and the others examined her carefully and confirmed that she was the daughter of the Shi family, their neighbor. Therefore, they released her midway. The girl's father, after learning what happened, was extremely angry and planned to sue them. After the neighbors and relatives tried their best to mediate, they apologized to the Shi family and settled the matter. He Jinzhang, the fiancée's father, was furious that the fiancé was unable to marry her and could have negotiated the matter, but instead, he resorted to such unreasonable actions, affecting the neighbor's daughter. He plans to file a lawsuit to dissolve the engagement.

Additional Winter Canal Tax to be Returned: It was decided at a county government meeting that an additional local expense budget of 8 jiao per shi would be temporarily collected under the heading of the 18th-year winter canal tax. From the start of the collection to January 29 of the 19th year, a total of 28,685 yuan was collected. It is now scheduled to begin on February 21. Those grain households who have already paid should bring their receipts to the original collection offices and receive the refund based on the receipts. The Finance Bureau has issued a public announcement to this effect.

Wuxi 83

Change of Warden at the Detention Center: Lin, President of the Higher Court, recently transferred Chen Chunyai, the warden of the Wuxi County Detention Center, to serve as prison administrator and warden of the Detention Center in Yangzhong County. Wang Nianci, the warden of the Fengxian County Detention Sub-center, has been transferred to Wuxi to take his place. County Magistrate Sun was notified of the instructions yesterday.

The Daji Steamer is Robbed at Dangkou: The Daji steamer of the Shanghai Laogongmao Shipping Bureau, which travels specifically to Changshu and other places, departed from Shanghai a few days ago. At about 4 PM the other day, the steamer was towing several other company boats, fully loaded with passengers, on its way to Changshu. Unexpectedly, when it reached the Ye Jiadun area near Dangkou in Nanyan City, this county, it was already late at night when a pirate ship appeared. More than ten bandits armed with handguns jumped on board and robbed the passengers. The ship's accounting room was also thoroughly searched. After about an hour, they left with their loot and fled. The ship's accounting room reported the incident to the 7th branch of the Public Security Bureau, requesting them to pursue the bandits. However, the bandits had already fled far away and could not be apprehended.

After the County Court Stopped Proceeding: It is said that the establishment of a county court in the county stopped because Lin, president of the Higher Court, insisted that the court should be located in the old Wuxi yamen and opposed the relocation to the City God Temple. It is now learned that Lian Liqing, Yang Yintan, and other members of the county bar association held a meeting at the Wuxi Hotel yesterday afternoon to discuss the matter. As a result, it was decided to elect representatives to petition the provincial government and the Higher Court to relocate the Public Security Bureau, which is currently using the old Wuxi yamen, to the original police station in front of the county government, so that the county court could be established as scheduled. Also, Dong Banggan, an adjudicator in this county, was ordered to transfer to serve as the head of the Nantong County Court. At the same time, Dong recommended Zhou, an adjudicator, (Zidun) to assist him in all matters. Dong went to Suzhou the other day to request instructions from Lin, president of the Higher Court, who ordered Zhou to continue serving in this county. Yang, an adjudicator from Wujiang County, has been transferred to Wuxi to take Dong's place. County Magistrate Sun was notified of the instructions by President Lin yesterday.

Report of a Strangled Male Corpse at Lihua Village: The Wuxi County Government yesterday received a report from Mao Jinshan, the Baojia head of Area 17, stating that an unidentified male corpse was found in a small river behind the Yansheng Temple in Lihua Village outside the North Gate, requesting an investigation. County Magistrate Sun ordered judicial secretary Wu Hou to bring the coroner Shen Guifang to investigate. The corpse was found to be about twenty years old, wearing a blue cloth short jacket and trousers, with a velvet close-fitting short shirt underneath, similar to a worker. His skin was white, but red. There were three rope marks wrapped around his throat and neck, indicating that he had been strangled to death before being thrown into the river. A corpse report was immediately filled out. Since there were no relatives of the deceased, photographs were taken and kept on file. The corpse was buried by the Baojia head.

Regimental Commander Xu Summoned to Nanjing: He Shicheng, the battalion commander of the 1st Battalion of the 31st Regiment of the 6th Division of the National Army stationed in Wuxi, was dismissed and sent to the Nanjing General Headquarters for interrogation after being accused of the Daiqiao Chamber of Commerce's purchase of guns. After half a month, Chiang Kai-shek secretly telegraphed Xu Dunrong, the regimental commander of the 31st Regiment stationed in Suzhou, to go to Nanjing immediately to inquire about the truth of the He case. In addition, Liang Zairong, the current battalion commander of the 1st Battalion of the 31st Regiment stationed in Wuxi, was ordered to return to the regimental headquarters. Gao Zhisong, a major staff officer of the 17th Brigade, has been appointed to take his place.

Fundraising to Build a New Prison: Yao Guozhang, the former chief secretary of the Jiangsu Higher Court, came to Wuxi to survey the site of the county court, but his main task was to investigate the current state of justice in various counties, especially the prisons. He determined that the Wuxi detention center and the detention branch were extremely overcrowded, with inmates having no place to sleep at night. Given the urgent need to build a new prison, he discussed the matter with County Magistrate Sun and decided to launch a fundraising committee to build a prison and initiate fundraising as soon as possible.

The Capture of the Bandit Leader who Robbed Weapons and Attacked the Police: Qiu Shizhen and five other bandit leaders who were running rampant in Dongxiang, robbing weapons and ammunition from police stations, and kidnapping police officers have been captured by the Qingxiang Bureau and sent to the city.

The Yangzhou Audit Office is Investigating Confiscated Fishing Salt: The Yangzhou Salt Affairs Audit Branch is investigating the 63 barrels of fishing salt that Peng Fenglai was captured with by the Lusi Anti-smuggling Camp in March of the 13th year of the Republic. The Tongtai branch office was ordered to track down and close the case.

County Magistrate Chen is Going to Haimen to Supervise the Burning of Opium: Chen Bu-chan, the magistrate of Nantong County, was ordered by the Department of Civil Affairs, representing Director Miao, to go to Haimen on the 25th to supervise the burning of opium.

The Inspection and Acceptance of the County Court's Buildings is Complete: Zhan Fengqi, commissioned by the Higher Court to inspect and accept the buildings of the county court, has completed the inspection and reported to President Lin, requesting that the court be opened as soon as possible to satisfy the people's hopes.

Organizing Local Public Institutions: Public institutions such as the Tongyi Museum and the Library have recently fallen into disrepair. The county government has decided at a county government meeting to urge the autonomous management office to allocate funds for repairs and earnestly organize them.

Zhenjiang 85

Department Order to Assist in the Arrest of Tong Zhengfu: The Jiangsu Department of Civil Affairs ordered that Tong Zhengfu, the captain of the 3rd squad of the Gaochun County Police Team, who released a bandit leader, has been dismissed three times but has refused to hand over his duties. After embezzling a large amount of military supplies, he fled. The department has issued an order to all county public security bureaus to assist in his arrest.

The Model Forest Begins Planting Trees: The First Forest Region Forestry Bureau of Jiangsu Province, following the provincial Capital Construction Committee's resolution, was ordered to vigorously plant trees on the mountains surrounding the city. After receiving the order, the bureau made active preparations and began spring planting on Taigu and Yihe Mountains. Zhou Guohua, the director of the bureau's 2nd section, led assistants and skilled foresters to the South Palace Temple on Jingxian Mountain outside the East Gate to oversee the afforestation of the model forest, and has hired short-term workers from the vicinity to begin planting trees.

The Progress of the Pond Work in the Four Townships: The Zhenjiang County Pond Work Committee was established last month and plans to provide work as relief by dredging the original ponds and ditches in the four townships to prevent drought. Recently, the people of the four townships have submitted reports on the length, width, and water capacity of their respective county ponds and ditches, as well as the steps and budget for dredging. The first committee meeting decided that all county pond work plans should be surveyed by the engineering section and then approved.

The Supervisor of Yangguan Customs Takes Office: The Office of the Supervisor of Yangguan Customs was ordered by the ministry to be placed under the jurisdiction of the General Inspectorate of Customs, changing the supervisor to the general director. It is now learned that the matters handled by the supervisor during his tenure have been concluded and the position of customs supervisor is still being held by Weng Shouchou, commissioned by the General Inspectorate of Customs.

Yangzhou 86

Petition to Increase Electricity Prices: Thirty-six industries, including the local Pisi industry, opposed Bao Yang Electric Light Company's illegal price increase and notified all consumers to stop paying electricity fees. Now, it has been reported that the industries are concerned about the company cutting off power and held a meeting to discuss the matter. Yesterday (22nd), they elected more than twenty representatives to petition the county, and prepared a petition and resolutions. County Magistrate Chen received them and, as a result, the county will submit the industries' opinions to the Department of Construction, which will forward them to the Construction Committee for review. The county has prevented the company from cutting off power. After leaving the county government, the representatives went to the Construction Bureau, where they were received by Director Wang, and the result was satisfactory.

Huzhou 87

Hejiabu is Robbed by Bandits and the Whole Town Goes on Strike: Hejiabu, located southwest of the city and bordering Heping Township in Changxing, is a notorious area for bandits. On the 20th of this month, at around 12:00 midnight, dozens of bandits speaking with a Hakka accent arrived, each carrying a handgun and flashlight, and robbed stores such as Tongtaixing and Wu Shufeng clean. Afterwards, they fired their guns as a show of force and left with a roar. Those villagers with some savings had already moved away, so they were not robbed. However, after this major blow, the shopkeepers, due to excessive losses, jointly decided to go on strike yesterday and reported to the county government, requesting the arrest of the bandits.

Gambling and Resisting Arrest, Injuring a Police Officer: Chen, the village chief of Ma Wu Village in Wuxing County, was gambling at home on the evening of the 20th. The Water Police learned of this and the squad leader Luo personally led several police officers to arrest him. Chen immediately ordered the crowd to resist arrest, injuring one police officer. Reinforcements of police officers were sent to bring Chen and the gamblers to the station. They were sent to the Wuxing Court yesterday for punishment.

Pinghu 88

The Patrol Chief Flees in Fear of Punishment: Gui Baoxi, the patrol chief of the Xinqiao Public Security Branch, was previously discovered by Director Wang to be having an affair with a woman in the town and was severely reprimanded. Recently, it was discovered by County Magistrate Fang Li that he had underreported the amount of opium seized in a raid on an opium den, and he was planning to punish him according to the law. Knowing that he could not escape the law, Gui fled with the woman a few days ago without a trace.

Guo Jianshi is Arrested by the Police: Guo Jianshi, a native of the county, who previously accused Lai Zhuangtao, a section chief of the Department of Finance, of accepting bribes, was arrested in Hangzhou for the crime of forging evidence. After being bailed out by a shop, Guo went into hiding. The police detectives learned of his whereabouts and arrested him, sending him to the Hangzhou County District Court for detention pending interrogation.

Meningitis Outbreak in Xincang Town: Fang Bao, the 14-year-old daughter of the late Zhou Hejun of Xincang Town, suddenly felt a headache the night before. Her mother thought it was a minor headache and did not care. Unexpectedly, by the next morning, she was barely breathing. A doctor was urgently called for examination, and it was diagnosed as meningitis. She died soon after. In the afternoon, her younger brother also suffered from the same symptoms and died within a few hours. Recently, there have been twenty or thirty cases of this disease in the town. According to doctors, the weather has been abnormal recently, making it easy for this disease to occur.

Pressing for Verification of Disaster Relief Public Bonds: Zhejiang Provincial Government Chairman Zhang Jingjiang telegraphed the National Government's Executive Yuan yesterday, stating that spring relief efforts in the province are nearing preparation. The plight of disaster victims is more severe than during the winter, and the number of affected households is greater than during the winter relief. There is an urgent need to raise funds for relief. Currently, there is no way to raise the relief funds, and the people are extremely anxious. Unless the Executive Yuan quickly passes and announces the province's disaster relief public bond case for fundraising, the millions of people in Zhejiang fear there will be no hope of survival.

Planning Immigration to Sanmen Bay: The Zhejiang Provincial Government believes that the land in Sanmen Bay is fertile, and reclamation will surely bring abundant resources. The area around it is over 110,000 mu, which can accommodate over 10,000 immigrants. Yesterday, a special letter was sent to the Northeast Immigration Committee for review and processing.

Bidding for Province-wide Sugar Tax: The original fixed amount for the Zhejiang province's sugar tax was 400,000 yuan, including surcharges. Now that the original contracted merchant's term has expired, rebidding will be conducted. The bidding is scheduled to open publicly at the Finance Department on March 3rd.

Silk Relief Conference: The Silk Relief Association, organized by twelve silk industry and commerce groups in Hangzhou, has been virtually suspended due to economic reasons. Implementing Price Evaluation: The Hangzhou Municipal Government, in accordance with commercial regulations, will review and decide on the quality and pricing of all kinds of commercial goods and products in the urban area. Province Approves Funds to Relieve Foil Workers: County Magistrate Tang of Shaoxing went to the provincial government a few days ago to request that 10% of the special tax surcharge on foil products be allocated to Shaoxing for the development of production enterprises, in order to help the foil workers' lives after the foil industry declines in the future. Chairman Zhang agreed to allocate the funds, which will be submitted to the provincial government for discussion within the month.

Increasing Land Tax Surcharge to Allocate Educational Expenses: Shaoxing's education funds have been severely strained since the rent reduction. County Magistrate Tang now plans to increase the land tax surcharge to allocate funds for the development of education. He has ordered the Director of the Education Bureau to properly draft methods for increasing the land tax education surcharge so that they can be submitted to the province for approval and implementation.

The Eleventh Army Headquarters Moves to Anhui: The Eleventh Army Commander Ma Hongkui's troops have been ordered to Anhui Province. The day before yesterday (20th) evening, the chief of staff and adjutant of the army headquarters, as well as the adjutant of the division headquarters, led the staff, adjutants, secretaries, quartermasters, military law officers, and military doctors from the eight departments of the army headquarters, as well as the training regiment, special service regiment, mortar company, pistol company, engineering company, and artillery company of the 64th Division, aboard the Yongxing and Jianguo steamers to Anhui.
